Show me the signs.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n \xe2\x80\x9cMy father!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n \xe2\x80\x9cFinally there was a quiet wedding at the Towers.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nEXPLANATORY\r\n\r\n\r\nThe Colonel Mulberry Sellers here re-introduced to the public is the\r\nsame person who appeared as _Eschol_ Sellers in the first edition of\r\nthe tale entitled \xe2\x80\x9cThe Gilded Age,\xe2\x80\x9d years ago, and as _Beriah_ Sellers\r\nin the subsequent editions of the same book, and finally as _Mulberry_\r\nSellers in the drama played afterward by John T. Raymond.\r\n\r\nThe name was changed from Eschol to Beriah to accommodate an Eschol\r\nSellers who rose up out of the vasty deeps of uncharted space and\r\npreferred his request\xe2\x80\x94backed by threat of a libel suit\xe2\x80\x94then went his\r\nway appeased, and came no more. In the play Beriah had to be dropped to\r\nsatisfy another member of the race, and Mulberry was substituted in the\r\nhope that the objectors would be tired by that time and let it pass\r\nunchallenged. So far it has occupied the field in peace; therefore we\r\nchance it again, feeling reasonably safe, this time, under shelter of\r\nthe statute of limitations.\r\n\r\nMARK TWAIN.\r\n\r\n\r\nHartford, 1891.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nTHE WEATHER IN THIS BOOK.\r\n\r\n\r\nNo weather will be found in this book. This is an attempt to pull a\r\nbook through without weather. It being the first attempt of the kind in\r\nfictitious literature, it may prove a failure, but it seemed worth the\r\nwhile of some dare-devil person to try it, and the author was in just\r\nthe mood.\r\n\r\nMany a reader who wanted to read a tale through was not able to do it\r\nbecause of delays on account of the weather. Nothing breaks up an\r\nauthor\xe2\x80\x99s progress like having to stop every few pages to fuss-up the\r\nweather. Thus it is plain that persistent intrusions of weather are bad\r\nfor both reader and author.\r\n\r\nOf course weather is necessary to a narrative of human experience. That\r\nis conceded. But it ought to be put where it will not be in the way;\r\nwhere it will not interrupt the flow of the narrative. And it ought to\r\nbe the ablest weather that can be had, not ignorant, poor-quality,\r\namateur weather. Weather is a literary specialty, and no untrained hand\r\ncan turn out a good article of it. The present author can do only a few\r\ntrifling ordinary kinds of weather, and he cannot do those very good.\r\nSo it has seemed wisest to borrow such weather as is necessary for the\r\nbook from qualified and recognized experts\xe2\x80\x94giving credit, of course.\r\nThis weather will be found over in the back part of the book, out of\r\nthe way. _See Appendix_. The reader is requested to turn over and help\r\nhimself from time to time as he goes along.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER I.\r\n\r\n\r\nIt is a matchless morning in rural England. On a fair hill we see a\r\nmajestic pile, the ivied walls and towers of Cholmondeley Castle, huge\r\nrelic and witness of the baronial grandeurs of the Middle Ages. This is\r\none of the seats of the Earl of Rossmore, K. G. G. C. B. K. C. M. G.,\r\netc., etc., etc., etc., etc., who possesses twenty-two thousand acres\r\nof English land, owns a parish in London with two thousand houses on\r\nits lease-roll, and struggles comfortably along on an income of two\r\nhundred thousand pounds a year. The father and founder of this proud\r\nold line was William the Conqueror his very self; the mother of it was\r\nnot inventoried in history by name, she being merely a random episode\r\nand inconsequential, like the tanner\xe2\x80\x99s daughter of Falaise.\r\n\r\nIn a breakfast room of the castle on this breezy fine morning there are\r\ntwo persons and the cooling remains of a deserted meal. One of these\r\npersons is the old lord, tall, erect, square-shouldered, white-haired,\r\nstern-browed, a man who shows character in every feature, attitude, and\r\nmovement, and carries his seventy years as easily as most men carry\r\nfifty. The other person is his only son and heir, a dreamy-eyed young\r\nfellow, who looks about twenty-six but is nearer thirty. Candor,\r\nkindliness, honesty, sincerity, simplicity, modesty\xe2\x80\x94it is easy to see\r\nthat these are cardinal traits of his character; and so when you have\r\nclothed him in the formidable components of his name, you somehow seem\r\nto be contemplating a lamb in armor: his name and style being the\r\nHonourable Kirkcudbright Llanover Marjoribanks Sellers\r\nViscount-Berkeley, of Cholmondeley Castle, Warwickshire. (Pronounced\r\nK\xe2\x80\x99koobry Thlanover Marshbanks Sellers Vycount Barkly, of Chumly Castle,\r\nWarrikshr.) He is standing by a great window, in an attitude suggestive\r\nof respectful attention to what his father is saying and equally\r\nrespectful dissent from the positions and arguments offered. The father\r\nwalks the floor as he talks, and his talk shows that his temper is away\r\nup toward summer heat.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSoft-spirited as you are, Berkeley, I am quite aware that when you\r\nhave once made up your mind to do a thing which your ideas of honor and\r\njustice require you to do, argument and reason are (for the time\r\nbeing,) wasted upon you\xe2\x80\x94yes, and ridicule; persuasion, supplication,\r\nand command as well. To my mind\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFather, if you will look at it without prejudice, without passion, you\r\nmust concede that I am not doing a rash thing, a thoughtless, wilful\r\nthing, with nothing substantial behind it to justify it. _I_ did not\r\ncreate the American claimant to the earldom of Rossmore; I did not hunt\r\nfor him, did not find him, did not obtrude him upon your notice. He\r\nfound himself, he injected himself into our lives\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd has made mine a purgatory for ten years with his tiresome letters,\r\nhis wordy reasonings, his acres of tedious evidence,\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhich you would never read, would never consent to read. Yet in common\r\nfairness he was entitled to a hearing. That hearing would either prove\r\nhe was the rightful earl\xe2\x80\x94in which case our course would be plain\xe2\x80\x94or it\r\nwould prove that he wasn\xe2\x80\x99t\xe2\x80\x94in which case our course would be equally\r\nplain. I have read his evidences, my lord. I have conned them well,\r\nstudied them patiently and thoroughly. The chain seems to be complete,\r\nno important link wanting. I believe he is the rightful earl.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I a usurper\xe2\x80\x94a\xe2\x80\x94nameless pauper, a tramp! Consider what you are\r\nsaying, sir.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFather, _if_ he is the rightful earl, would you, could you\xe2\x80\x94that fact\r\nbeing established\xe2\x80\x94consent to keep his titles and his properties from\r\nhim a day, an hour, a minute?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are talking nonsense\xe2\x80\x94nonsense\xe2\x80\x94lurid idiocy! Now, listen to me. I\r\nwill make a confession\xe2\x80\x94if you wish to call it by that name. I did not\r\nread those evidences because I had no occasion to\xe2\x80\x94I was made familiar\r\nwith them in the time of this claimant\xe2\x80\x99s father and of my own father\r\nforty years ago. This fellow\xe2\x80\x99s predecessors have kept mine more or less\r\nfamiliar with them for close upon a hundred and fifty years. The truth\r\nis, the rightful heir did go to America, with the Fairfax heir or about\r\nthe same time\xe2\x80\x94but disappeared\xe2\x80\x94somewhere in the wilds of Virginia, got\r\nmarried, and began to breed savages for the Claimant market; wrote no\r\nletters home; was supposed to be dead; his younger brother softly took\r\npossession; presently the American did die, and straightway his eldest\r\nproduct put in his claim\xe2\x80\x94by letter\xe2\x80\x94letter still in existence\xe2\x80\x94and died\r\nbefore the uncle in-possession found time\xe2\x80\x94or maybe\r\ninclination\xe2\x80\x94to\xe2\x80\x94answer. The infant son of that eldest product grew\r\nup\xe2\x80\x94long interval, you see\xe2\x80\x94and _he_ took to writing letters and\r\nfurnishing evidences. Well, successor after successor has done the\r\nsame, down to the present idiot. It was a succession of paupers; not\r\none of them was ever able to pay his passage to England or institute\r\nsuit. The Fairfaxes kept their lordship alive, and so they have never\r\nlost it to this day, although they live in Maryland; their friend lost\r\nhis by his own neglect. You perceive now, that the facts in this case\r\nbring us to precisely this result: morally the American tramp _is_\r\nrightful earl of Rossmore; legally he has no more right than his dog.\r\nThere now\xe2\x80\x94are you satisfied?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThere was a pause, then the son glanced at the crest carved in the\r\ngreat oaken mantel and said, with a regretful note in his voice:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSince the introduction of heraldic symbols,\xe2\x80\x94the motto of this house\r\nhas been _Suum cuique_\xe2\x80\x94to every man his own. By your own intrepidly\r\nfrank confession, my lord, it is become a sarcasm: If Simon Lathers\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cKeep that exasperating name to yourself! For ten years it has pestered\r\nmy eye\xe2\x80\x94and tortured my ear; till at last my very footfalls time\r\nthemselves to the brain-racking rhythm of _Simon Lathers!\xe2\x80\x94Simon\r\nLathers! \xe2\x80\x94Simon Lathers!_ And now, to make its presence in my soul\r\neternal, immortal, imperishable, you have resolved to\xe2\x80\x94to\xe2\x80\x94what is it you\r\nhave resolved to do?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo go to Simon Lathers, in America, and change places with him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat? See here\r\n\xe2\x80\x94have you been training with that ass again\xe2\x80\x94that radical, if you prefer\r\nthe term, though the words are synonymous\xe2\x80\x94Lord Tanzy, of Tollmache?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe son did not reply, and the old lord continued:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, you confess. That puppy, that shame to his birth and caste, who\r\nholds all hereditary lordships and privilege to be usurpation, all\r\nnobility a tinsel sham, all aristocratic institutions a fraud, all\r\ninequalities in rank a legalized crime and an infamy, and no bread\r\nhonest bread that a man doesn\xe2\x80\x99t earn by his own work\xe2\x80\x94_work_, pah!\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94and\r\nthe old patrician brushed imaginary labor-dirt from his white hands.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou have come to hold just those opinions yourself, I suppose,\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94he\r\nadded with a sneer.\r\n\r\nA faint flush in the younger man\xe2\x80\x99s cheek told that the shot had hit and\r\nhurt; but he answered with dignity:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have. I say it without shame\xe2\x80\x94I feel none. And now my reason for\r\nresolving to renounce my heirship without resistance is explained. I\r\nwish to retire from what to me is a false existence, a false position,\r\nand begin my life over again\xe2\x80\x94begin it right\xe2\x80\x94begin it on the level of\r\nmere manhood, unassisted by factitious aids, and succeed or fail by\r\npure merit or the want of it. I will go to America, where all men are\r\nequal and all have an equal chance; I will live or die, sink or swim,\r\nwin or lose as just a man\xe2\x80\x94that alone, and not a single helping gaud or\r\nfiction back of it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHear, hear!\xe2\x80\x9d The two men looked each other steadily in the eye a\r\nmoment or two, then the elder one added, musingly, \xe2\x80\x9cAb-so-lutely\r\ncra-zy\xe2\x80\x94ab-solutely!\xe2\x80\x9d After another silence, he said, as one who, long\r\ntroubled by clouds, detects a ray of sunshine, \xe2\x80\x9cWell, there will be one\r\nsatisfaction\xe2\x80\x94Simon Lathers will come here to enter into his own, and I\r\nwill drown him in the horsepond. The poor devil\xe2\x80\x94always so humble in his\r\nletters, so pitiful, so deferential; so steeped in reverence for our\r\ngreat line and lofty-station; so anxious to placate us, so prayerful\r\nfor recognition as a relative, a bearer in his veins of our sacred\r\nblood\xe2\x80\x94and withal so poor, so needy, so threadbare and pauper-shod as to\r\nraiment, so despised, so laughed at for his silly claimantship by the\r\nlewd American scum around him\xe2\x80\x94ah, the vulgar, crawling, insufferable\r\ntramp! To read one of his cringing, nauseating letters\xe2\x80\x94well?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThis to a splendid flunkey, all in inflamed plush and buttons and\r\nknee-breeches as to his trunk, and a glinting white frost-work of\r\nground-glass paste as to his head, who stood with his heels together\r\nand the upper half of him bent forward, a salver in his hands:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe letters, my lord.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMy lord took them, and the servant disappeared.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAmong the rest, an American letter. From the tramp, of course. Jove,\r\nbut here\xe2\x80\x99s a change! No brown paper envelope this time, filched from a\r\nshop, and carrying the shop\xe2\x80\x99s advertisement in the corner. Oh, no, a\r\nproper enough envelope\xe2\x80\x94with a most ostentatiously broad mourning\r\nborder\xe2\x80\x94for his cat, perhaps, since he was a bachelor\xe2\x80\x94and fastened with\r\nred wax\xe2\x80\x94a batch of it as big as a half-crown\xe2\x80\x94and\xe2\x80\x94and\xe2\x80\x94our crest for a\r\nseal!\xe2\x80\x94motto and all. STREET,\r\nWASHINGTON, May 2.\r\n\r\n\r\n_My Lord_\xe2\x80\x94\r\nIt is my painful duty to announce to you that the head of our\r\nillustrious house is no more\xe2\x80\x94The Right Honourable, The Most Noble, The\r\nMost Puissant Simon Lathers Lord Rossmore having departed this life\r\n(\xe2\x80\x9cGone at last\xe2\x80\x94this is unspeakably precious news, my son,\xe2\x80\x9d) at his seat\r\nin the environs of the hamlet of Duffy\xe2\x80\x99s Corners in the grand old State\r\nof Arkansas,\xe2\x80\x94and his twin brother with him, both being crushed by a log\r\nat a smoke-house-raising, owing to carelessness on the part of all\r\npresent, referable to over-confidence and gaiety induced by overplus of\r\nsour-mash\xe2\x80\x94(\xe2\x80\x9cExtolled be sour-mash, whatever that may be, eh Berkeley?\xe2\x80\x9d)\r\nfive days ago, with no scion of our ancient race present to close his\r\neyes and inter him with the honors due his historic name and lofty\r\nrank\xe2\x80\x94in fact, he is on the ice yet, him and his brother\xe2\x80\x94friends took up\r\na collection for it. But I shall take immediate occasion to have their\r\nnoble remains shipped to you (\xe2\x80\x9cGreat heavens!\xe2\x80\x9d) for interment, with due\r\nceremonies and solemnities, in the family vault or mausoleum of our\r\nhouse. Meantime I shall put up a pair of hatchments on my house-front,\r\nand you will of course do the same at your several seats.\r\n\r\nI have also to remind you that by this sad disaster I as sole heir,\r\ninherit and become seized of all the titles, honors, lands, and goods\r\nof our lamented relative, and must of necessity, painful as the duty\r\nis, shortly require at the bar of the Lords restitution of these\r\ndignities and properties, now illegally enjoyed by your titular\r\nlordship.\r\n\r\nWith assurance of my distinguished consideration and warm cousinly\r\nregard, I remain\r\n\r\nYour titular lordship\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nMost obedient servant,\r\n_Mulberry Sellers Earl Rossmore_.\r\n\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIm-mense! Come, this one\xe2\x80\x99s interesting. Why, Berkeley, his breezy\r\nimpudence is\xe2\x80\x94is\xe2\x80\x94why, it\xe2\x80\x99s colossal, it\xe2\x80\x99s sublime.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, this one doesn\xe2\x80\x99t seem to cringe much.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCringe\xe2\x80\x94why, he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t know the meaning of the word. Hatchments! To\r\ncommemorate that sniveling tramp and his, fraternal duplicate. And he\r\nis going to send me the remains. What a name! _Mulberry_\r\nSellers\xe2\x80\x94there\xe2\x80\x99s music for you, Simon Lathers\xe2\x80\x94Mulberry Sellers\xe2\x80\x94Mulberry\r\nSellers\xe2\x80\x94Simon Lathers. Sounds like machinery working and churning.\r\nSimon Lathers, Mulberry Sel\xe2\x80\x94Are you going?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf I have your leave, father.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe old gentleman stood musing some time, after his son was gone. Yas!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER II.\r\n\r\n\r\np027.jpg (32K)\r\n\r\nColonel Mulberry Sellers\xe2\x80\x94this was some days before he wrote his letter\r\nto Lord Rossmore\xe2\x80\x94was seated in his \xe2\x80\x9clibrary,\xe2\x80\x9d which was also his\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cdrawing-room\xe2\x80\x9d and was also his \xe2\x80\x9cpicture gallery\xe2\x80\x9d and likewise his\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cwork-shop.\xe2\x80\x9d Sometimes he called it by one of these names, sometimes by\r\nanother, according to occasion and circumstance. He was constructing\r\nwhat seemed to be some kind of a frail mechanical toy; and was\r\napparently very much interested in his work. He was a white-headed man,\r\nnow, but otherwise he was as young, alert, buoyant, visionary and\r\nenterprising as ever. His loving old wife sat near by, contentedly\r\nknitting and thinking, with a cat asleep in her lap. The room was\r\nlarge, light, and had a comfortable look, in fact a home-like look,\r\nthough the furniture was of a humble sort and not over abundant, and\r\nthe knickknacks and things that go to adorn a living-room not plenty\r\nand not costly. But there were natural flowers, and there was an\r\nabstract and unclassifiable something about the place which betrayed\r\nthe presence in the house of somebody with a happy taste and an\r\neffective touch.\r\n\r\nEven the deadly chromos on the walls were somehow without offence; in\r\nfact they seemed to belong there and to add an attraction to the room\xe2\x80\x94a\r\nfascination, anyway; for whoever got his eye on one of them was like to\r\ngaze and suffer till he died\xe2\x80\x94you have seen that kind of pictures. Some\r\nof these terrors were landscapes, some libeled the sea, some were\r\nostensible portraits, all were crimes. All the portraits were\r\nrecognizable as dead Americans of distinction, and yet, through\r\nlabeling added, by a daring hand, they were all doing duty here as\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cEarls of Rossmore.\xe2\x80\x9d The newest one had left the works as Andrew\r\nJackson, but was doing its best now, as \xe2\x80\x9cSimon Lathers Lord Rossmore,\r\nPresent Earl.\xe2\x80\x9d On one wall was a cheap old railroad map of\r\nWarwickshire. This had been newly labeled \xe2\x80\x9cThe Rossmore Estates.\xe2\x80\x9d On\r\nthe opposite wall was another map, and this was the most imposing\r\ndecoration of the establishment and the first to catch a stranger\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nattention, because of its great size. It had a\r\nneglected yard around it, with paling fence that needed straightening\r\nup, in places, and a gate that would stay shut. By the door-post were\r\nseveral modest tin signs. \xe2\x80\x9cCol. Mulberry Sellers, Attorney at Law and\r\nClaim Agent,\xe2\x80\x9d was the principal one. One learned from the others that\r\nthe Colonel was a Materializer, a Hypnotizer, a Mind-Cure dabbler; and\r\nso on. Yes, and oh, the changes\r\nthat\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThere was a sudden catch of her voice and a trembling of the lip, the\r\nmen waiting reverently for her to get command of herself and go on; but\r\nafter a little struggle she turned away, with her apron to her eyes,\r\nand softly disappeared.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeeing you made her think of the children, poor thing\xe2\x80\x94dear, dear,\r\nthey\xe2\x80\x99re all dead but the youngest.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut banish care, it\xe2\x80\x99s no time for it now\xe2\x80\x94on with the dance, let joy be\r\nunconfined is my motto, whether there\xe2\x80\x99s any dance to dance; or any joy\r\nto unconfine\xe2\x80\x94you\xe2\x80\x99ll be the healthier for it every time,\xe2\x80\x94every time,\r\nWashington\xe2\x80\x94it\xe2\x80\x99s my experience, and I\xe2\x80\x99ve seen a good deal of this world.\r\nCome\xe2\x80\x94where have you disappeared to all these years, and are you from\r\nthere, now, or where are you from?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t quite think you would ever guess, Colonel. Office established in the time of the Revolution, last century.\r\nThe musket-flints for the military posts were supplied from the\r\ncapitol. They do it yet; for although the flint-arm has gone out and\r\nthe forts have tumbled down, the decree hasn\xe2\x80\x99t been repealed\xe2\x80\x94been\r\noverlooked and forgotten, you see\xe2\x80\x94and so the vacancies where old\r\nTiconderoga and others used to stand, still get their six quarts of\r\ngun-flints a year just the same.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington said musingly after a pause:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow strange it seems\xe2\x80\x94to start for Minister to England at twenty\r\nthousand a year and fail for flintpicker at\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThree dollars a week. It\xe2\x80\x99s human life, Washington\xe2\x80\x94just an epitome of\r\nhuman ambition, and struggle, and the outcome: you aim for the palace\r\nand get drowned in the sewer.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThere was another meditative silence. Then Washington said, with\r\nearnest compassion in his voice\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd so, after coming here, against your inclination, to satisfy your\r\nsense of patriotic duty and appease a selfish public clamor, you get\r\nabsolutely nothing for it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing?\xe2\x80\x9d The Colonel had to get up and stand, to get room for his\r\namazement to expand. \xe2\x80\x9c_Nothing_, Washington? I ask you this: to be a\r\nperpetual Member and the _only_ Perpetual Member of a Diplomatic Body\r\naccredited to the greatest country on earth do you call that nothing?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIt was Washington\xe2\x80\x99s turn to be amazed. He was stricken dumb; but the\r\nwide-eyed wonder, the reverent admiration expressed in his face were\r\nmore eloquent than any words could have been. The Colonel\xe2\x80\x99s wounded\r\nspirit was healed and he resumed his seat pleased and content. He\r\nleaned forward and said impressively:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat was due to a man who had become forever conspicuous by an\r\nexperience without precedent in the history of the world?\xe2\x80\x94a man made\r\npermanently and diplomatically sacred, so to speak, by having been\r\nconnected, temporarily, through solicitation, with every single\r\ndiplomatic post in the roster of this government, from Envoy\r\nExtraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary to the Court of St. James\r\nall the way down to Consul to a guano rock in the Strait of\r\nSunda\xe2\x80\x94salary payable in guano\xe2\x80\x94which disappeared by volcanic convulsion\r\nthe day before they got down to my name in the list of applicants.\r\nCertainly something august enough to be answerable to the size of this\r\nunique and memorable experience was my due, and I got it. By the common\r\nvoice of this community, by acclamation of the people, that mighty\r\nutterance which brushes aside laws and legislation, and from whose\r\ndecrees there is no appeal, I was named Perpetual Member of the\r\nDiplomatic Body representing the multifarious sovereignties and\r\ncivilizations of the globe near the republican court of the United\r\nStates of America. And they brought me home with a torchlight\r\nprocession.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is wonderful, Colonel, simply wonderful.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s the loftiest official position in the whole earth.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI should think so\xe2\x80\x94and the most commanding.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou have named the word. Think of it. I frown, and there is war; I\r\nsmile, and contending nations lay down their arms.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is awful. The responsibility, I mean.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is nothing. Responsibility is no burden to me; I am used to it;\r\nhave always been used to it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd the work\xe2\x80\x94the work! Do you have to attend all the sittings?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho, I? Does the Emperor of Russia attend the conclaves of the\r\ngovernors of the provinces? He sits at home, and indicates his\r\npleasure.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington was silent a moment, then a deep sigh escaped him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow proud I was an hour ago; how paltry seems my little promotion now!\r\nColonel, the reason I came to Washington is,\xe2\x80\x94I am Congressional\r\nDelegate from Cherokee Strip!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe Colonel sprang to his feet and broke out with prodigious\r\nenthusiasm:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGive me your hand, my boy\xe2\x80\x94this is immense news! I congratulate you\r\nwith all my heart. My prophecies stand confirmed. I always said it was\r\nin you. I always said you were born for high distinction and would\r\nachieve it. You ask Polly if I didn\xe2\x80\x99t.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington was dazed by this most unexpected demonstration.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, Colonel, there\xe2\x80\x99s nothing _to_ it. That little narrow, desolate,\r\nunpeopled, oblong streak of grass and gravel, lost in the remote wastes\r\nof the vast continent\xe2\x80\x94why, it\xe2\x80\x99s like representing a billiard table\xe2\x80\x94a\r\ndiscarded one.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTut-tut, it\xe2\x80\x99s a great, it\xe2\x80\x99s a staving preferment, and just opulent\r\nwith influence here.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShucks, Colonel, I haven\xe2\x80\x99t even a vote.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s nothing; you can make speeches.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, I can\xe2\x80\x99t. The population\xe2\x80\x99s only two hundred\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s all right, that\xe2\x80\x99s all right\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd they hadn\xe2\x80\x99t any right to elect me; we\xe2\x80\x99re not even a territory,\r\nthere\xe2\x80\x99s no Organic Act, the government hasn\xe2\x80\x99t any official knowledge of\r\nus whatever.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNever mind about that; I\xe2\x80\x99ll fix that. I\xe2\x80\x99ll rush the thing through,\r\nI\xe2\x80\x99ll get you organized in no time.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Will_ you, Colonel?\xe2\x80\x94it\xe2\x80\x99s _too_ good of you; but it\xe2\x80\x99s just your old\r\nsterling self, the same old ever-faithful friend,\xe2\x80\x9d and the grateful\r\ntears welled up in Washington\xe2\x80\x99s eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s just as good as done, my boy, just as good as done. Shake hands.\r\nWe\xe2\x80\x99ll hitch teams together, you and I, and we\xe2\x80\x99ll make things hum!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER III.\r\n\r\n\r\nMrs. Sellers returned, now, with her composure restored, and began to\r\nask after Hawkins\xe2\x80\x99s wife, and about his children, and the number of\r\nthem, and so on, and her examination of the witness resulted in a\r\ncircumstantial history of the family\xe2\x80\x99s ups and downs and driftings to\r\nand fro in the far West during the previous fifteen years. There was a\r\nmessage, now, from out back, and Colonel Sellers went out there in\r\nanswer to it. Hawkins took this opportunity to ask how the world had\r\nbeen using the Colonel during the past half-generation.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, it\xe2\x80\x99s been using him just the same; it couldn\xe2\x80\x99t change its way of\r\nusing him if it wanted to, for he wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t let it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can easily believe that, Mrs. Sellers.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, you see, he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t change, himself\xe2\x80\x94not the least little bit in\r\nthe world\xe2\x80\x94he\xe2\x80\x99s always Mulberry Sellers.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can see _that_ plain enough.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cJust the same old scheming, generous, good-hearted, moonshiny,\r\nhopeful, no-account failure he always was, and still everybody likes\r\nhim just as well as if he was the shiningest success.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey always did: and it was natural, because he was so obliging and\r\naccommodating, and had something about him that made it kind of easy to\r\nask help of him, or favors\xe2\x80\x94you didn\xe2\x80\x99t feel shy, you know, or have that\r\nwish\xe2\x80\x94you\xe2\x80\x94didn\xe2\x80\x99t\xe2\x80\x94have\xe2\x80\x94to\xe2\x80\x94try feeling that you have with other people.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s just so, yet; and a body wonders at it, too, because he\xe2\x80\x99s been\r\nshamefully treated, many times, by people that had used him for a\r\nladder to climb up by, and then kicked him down when they didn\xe2\x80\x99t need\r\nhim any more. For a time you can see he\xe2\x80\x99s hurt, his pride\xe2\x80\x99s wounded,\r\nbecause he shrinks away from that thing and don\xe2\x80\x99t want to talk about\r\nit\xe2\x80\x94and so I used to think _now_ he\xe2\x80\x99s learned something and he\xe2\x80\x99ll be\r\nmore careful hereafter\xe2\x80\x94but laws! in a couple of weeks he\xe2\x80\x99s forgotten\r\nall about it, and any selfish tramp out of nobody knows where can come\r\nand put up a poor mouth and walk right into his heart with his boots\r\non.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt must try your patience pretty sharply sometimes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\np038.jpg (36K)\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, no, I\xe2\x80\x99m used to it; and I\xe2\x80\x99d rather have him so than the other way.\r\nWhen I call him a failure, I mean to the world he\xe2\x80\x99s a failure; he isn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nto me. I don\xe2\x80\x99t know as I want him different much different, anyway. I\r\nhave to scold him some, snarl at him, you might even call it, but I\r\nreckon I\xe2\x80\x99d do that just the same, if he was different\xe2\x80\x94it\xe2\x80\x99s my make. But\r\nI\xe2\x80\x99m a good deal less snarly and more contented when he\xe2\x80\x99s a failure than\r\nI am when he isn\xe2\x80\x99t.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen he isn\xe2\x80\x99t always a failure,\xe2\x80\x9d said Hawking, brightening.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHim? Oh, bless you, no. He makes a strike, as he calls it, from time\r\nto time. Then\xe2\x80\x99s my time to fret and fuss. For the money just\r\nflies\xe2\x80\x94first come first served. Straight off, he loads up the house with\r\ncripples and idiots and stray cats and all the different kinds of poor\r\nwrecks that other people don\xe2\x80\x99t want and he _does_, and then when the\r\npoverty comes again I\xe2\x80\x99ve _got_ to clear the most of them out or we\xe2\x80\x99d\r\nstarve; and that distresses him, and me the same, of course.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHere\xe2\x80\x99s old Dan\xe2\x80\x99l and old Jinny, that the sheriff sold south one of the\r\ntimes that we got bankrupted before the war\xe2\x80\x94they came wandering back\r\nafter the peace, worn out and used up on the cotton plantations,\r\nhelpless, and not another lick of work left in their old hides for the\r\nrest of this earthly pilgrimage\xe2\x80\x94and we so pinched, _oh_ so pinched for\r\nthe very crumbs to keep life in us, and he just flung the door wide,\r\nand the way he received them you\xe2\x80\x99d have thought they had come straight\r\ndown from heaven in answer to prayer. I took him one side and said,\r\n\xe2\x80\x98Mulberry we can\xe2\x80\x99t have them\xe2\x80\x94we\xe2\x80\x99ve nothing for ourselves\xe2\x80\x94we can\xe2\x80\x99t feed\r\nthem.\xe2\x80\x99 He looked at me kind of hurt, and said, \xe2\x80\x98Turn them out?\xe2\x80\x94and\r\nthey\xe2\x80\x99ve come to me just as confident and trusting as\xe2\x80\x94as\xe2\x80\x94why Polly, I\r\nmust have _bought_ that confidence sometime or other a long time ago,\r\nand given my note, so to speak\xe2\x80\x94you don\xe2\x80\x99t get such things as a\r\n_gift_\xe2\x80\x94and how am I going to go back on a debt like that? And you see,\r\nthey\xe2\x80\x99re so poor, and old, and friendless, and\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x99 But I was ashamed by\r\nthat time, and shut him off, and somehow felt a new courage in me, and\r\nso I said, softly, \xe2\x80\x98We\xe2\x80\x99ll keep them\xe2\x80\x94the Lord will provide.\xe2\x80\x99 He was\r\nglad, and started to blurt out one of those over-confident speeches of\r\nhis, but checked himself in time, and said humbly, \xe2\x80\x98_I_ will, anyway.\xe2\x80\x99\r\nIt was years and years and years ago. Well, you see those old wrecks\r\nare here yet.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut don\xe2\x80\x99t they do your housework?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLaws! The idea. They would if they could, poor old things, and perhaps\r\nthey think they _do_ do some of it. But it\xe2\x80\x99s a superstition. Dan\xe2\x80\x99l\r\nwaits on the front door, and sometimes goes on an errand; and sometimes\r\nyou\xe2\x80\x99ll see one or both of them letting on to dust around in here\xe2\x80\x94but\r\nthat\xe2\x80\x99s because there\xe2\x80\x99s something they want to hear about and mix their\r\ngabble into. And they\xe2\x80\x99re always around at meals, for the same reason.\r\nBut the fact is, we have to keep a young negro girl just to take care\r\nof _them_, and a negro woman to do the housework and _help_ take care\r\nof them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, they ought to be tolerably happy, I should think.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s no name for it. They quarrel together pretty much all the\r\ntime\xe2\x80\x94most always about religion, because Dan\xe2\x80\x99l\xe2\x80\x99s a Dunker Baptist and\r\nJinny\xe2\x80\x99s a shouting Methodist, and Jinny believes in special Providences\r\nand Dan\xe2\x80\x99l don\xe2\x80\x99t, because he thinks he\xe2\x80\x99s a kind of a free-thinker\xe2\x80\x94and\r\nthey play and sing plantation hymns together, and talk and chatter just\r\neternally and forever, and are sincerely fond of each other and think\r\nthe world of Mulberry, and he puts up patiently with all their spoiled\r\nways and foolishness, and so\xe2\x80\x94ah, well, they\xe2\x80\x99re happy enough if it comes\r\nto that. And I don\xe2\x80\x99t mind\xe2\x80\x94I\xe2\x80\x99ve got used to it. I can get used to\r\nanything, with Mulberry to help; and the fact is, I don\xe2\x80\x99t much care\r\nwhat happens, so long as he\xe2\x80\x99s spared to me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, here\xe2\x80\x99s to him, and hoping he\xe2\x80\x99ll make another strike soon.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd rake in the lame, the halt and the blind, and turn the house into\r\na hospital again? It\xe2\x80\x99s what he would do. I\xe2\x80\x99ve seen aplenty of that and\r\nmore. No, Washington, I want his strikes to be mighty moderate ones the\r\nrest of the way down the vale.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, then, big strike or little strike, or no strike at all, here\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nhoping he\xe2\x80\x99ll never lack for friends\xe2\x80\x94and I don\xe2\x80\x99t reckon he ever will\r\nwhile there\xe2\x80\x99s people around who know enough to\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHim lack for friends!\xe2\x80\x9d and she tilted her head up with a frank\r\npride\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9cwhy, Washington, you can\xe2\x80\x99t name a man that\xe2\x80\x99s anybody that isn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nfond of him. I\xe2\x80\x99ll tell you privately, that I\xe2\x80\x99ve had Satan\xe2\x80\x99s own time to\r\nkeep them from appointing him to some office or other. They knew he\xe2\x80\x99d\r\nno business with an office, just as well as I did, but he\xe2\x80\x99s the hardest\r\nman to refuse anything to a body ever saw. Mulberry Sellers with an\r\noffice! laws goodness, you know what that would be like. Why, they\xe2\x80\x99d\r\ncome from the ends of the earth to see a circus like that. I\xe2\x80\x99d just as\r\nlieves be married to Niagara Falls, and done with it.\xe2\x80\x9d After a\r\nreflective pause she added\xe2\x80\x94having wandered back, in the interval, to\r\nthe remark that had been her text: \xe2\x80\x9cFriends?\xe2\x80\x94oh, indeed, no man ever\r\nhad more; and _such_ friends: Grant, Sherman, Sheridan, Johnston,\r\nLongstreet, Lee\xe2\x80\x94many\xe2\x80\x99s the time they\xe2\x80\x99ve sat in that chair you\xe2\x80\x99re\r\nsitting in\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d Hawkins was out of it instantly, and contemplating it with\r\na reverential surprise, and with the awed sense of having trodden shod\r\nupon holy ground\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_They!_\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, indeed, yes, a many and a many a time.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe continued to gaze at the chair fascinated, magnetized; and for once\r\nin his life that continental stretch of dry prairie which stood for his\r\nimagination was afire, and across it was marching a slanting flamefront\r\nthat joined its wide horizons together and smothered the skies with\r\nsmoke. He was experiencing what one or another drowsing, geographically\r\nignorant alien experiences every day in the year when he turns a dull\r\nand indifferent eye out of the car window and it falls upon a certain\r\nstation-sign which reads \xe2\x80\x9cStratford-on-Avon!\xe2\x80\x9d Mrs. Sellers went\r\ngossiping comfortably along:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, they like to hear him talk, especially if their load is getting\r\nrather heavy on one shoulder and they want to shift it. He\xe2\x80\x99s all air,\r\nyou know,\xe2\x80\x94breeze, you may say\xe2\x80\x94and he freshens them up; it\xe2\x80\x99s a trip to\r\nthe country, they say. Many a time he\xe2\x80\x99s made General Grant laugh\xe2\x80\x94and\r\nthat\xe2\x80\x99s a tidy job, I can tell you, and as for Sheridan, his eye lights\r\nup and he listens to Mulberry Sellers the same as if he was artillery.\r\nYou see, the charm about Mulberry is, he is so catholic and\r\nunprejudiced that he fits in anywhere and everywhere. It makes him\r\npowerful good company, and as popular as scandal. You go to the White\r\nHouse when the President\xe2\x80\x99s holding a general reception\xe2\x80\x94sometime when\r\nMulberry\xe2\x80\x99s there. Why, dear me, _you_ can\xe2\x80\x99t tell which of them it is\r\nthat\xe2\x80\x99s holding that reception.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, he certainly is a remarkable man\xe2\x80\x94and he always was. Is he\r\nreligious?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cClear to his marrow\xe2\x80\x94does more thinking and reading on that subject\r\nthan any other except Russia and Siberia: thrashes around over the\r\nwhole field, too; nothing bigoted about him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is his religion?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d She stopped, and was lost for a moment or two in thinking, then\r\nshe said, with simplicity, \xe2\x80\x9cI think he was a Mohammedan or something\r\nlast week.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington started down town, now, to bring his trunk, for the\r\nhospitable Sellerses would listen to no excuses; their house must be\r\nhis home during the session. The Colonel returned presently and resumed\r\nwork upon his plaything. It was finished when Washington got back.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere it is,\xe2\x80\x9d said the Colonel, \xe2\x80\x9call finished.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is it for, Colonel?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, it\xe2\x80\x99s just a trifle. Toy to amuse the children.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington examined it.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt seems to be a puzzle.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, that\xe2\x80\x99s what it is. I call it Pigs in the Clover. Put them in\xe2\x80\x94see\r\nif you can put them in the pen.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAfter many failures Washington succeeded, and was as pleased as a\r\nchild.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s wonderfully ingenious, Colonel, it\xe2\x80\x99s ever so clever and\r\ninteresting\xe2\x80\x94why, I could play with it all day. What are you going to do\r\nwith it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, nothing. Patent it and throw it aside.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t you do anything of the kind. There\xe2\x80\x99s money in that thing.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nA compassionate look traveled over the Colonel\xe2\x80\x99s countenance, and he\r\nsaid:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMoney\xe2\x80\x94yes; pin money: a couple of hundred thousand, perhaps. Not\r\nmore.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington\xe2\x80\x99s eyes blazed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA couple of hundred thousand dollars! do you call that pin money?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe colonel rose and tip-toed his way across the room, closed a door\r\nthat was slightly ajar, tip-toed his way to his seat again, and said,\r\nunder his breath:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou can keep a secret?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington nodded his affirmative, he was too awed to speak.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou have heard of materialization\xe2\x80\x94materialization of departed\r\nspirits?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington had heard of it.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd probably didn\xe2\x80\x99t believe in it; and quite right, too. The thing as\r\npractised by ignorant charlatans is unworthy of attention or\r\nrespect\xe2\x80\x94where there\xe2\x80\x99s a dim light and a dark cabinet, and a parcel of\r\nsentimental gulls gathered together, with their faith and their\r\nshudders and their tears all ready, and one and the same fatty\r\ndegeneration of protoplasm and humbug comes out and materializes\r\nhimself into anybody you want, grandmother, grandchild, brother-in-law,\r\nWitch of Endor, John Milton, Siamese twins, Peter the Great, and all\r\nsuch frantic nonsense\xe2\x80\x94no, that is all foolish and pitiful. But when a\r\nman that is competent brings the vast powers of _science_ to bear, it\xe2\x80\x99s\r\na different matter, a totally different matter, you see. The spectre\r\nthat answers _that_ call has come to stay. Do you note the commercial\r\nvalue of that detail?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, I\xe2\x80\x94the\xe2\x80\x94the truth is, that I don\xe2\x80\x99t quite know that I do. Do you\r\nmean that such, being permanent, not transitory, would give more\r\ngeneral satisfaction, and so enhance the price\xe2\x80\x94of tickets to the show\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShow? Folly\xe2\x80\x94listen to me; and get a good grip on your breath, for you\r\nare going to need it. Within three days I shall have completed my\r\nmethod, and then\xe2\x80\x94let the world stand aghast, for it shall see marvels.\r\nWashington, within three days\xe2\x80\x94ten at the outside\xe2\x80\x94you shall see me call\r\nthe dead of any century, and they will arise and walk. Walk?\xe2\x80\x94they shall\r\nwalk forever, and never die again. Walk with all the muscle and spring\r\nof their pristine vigor.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cColonel! Indeed it does take one\xe2\x80\x99s breath away.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Now_ do you see the money that\xe2\x80\x99s in it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m\xe2\x80\x94well, I\xe2\x80\x99m\xe2\x80\x94not really sure that I do.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGreat Scott, look here. I shall have a monopoly; they\xe2\x80\x99ll all belong to\r\nme, won\xe2\x80\x99t they? Two thousand policemen in the city of New York. Wages,\r\nfour dollars a day. I\xe2\x80\x99ll replace them with dead ones at half the\r\nmoney.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, prodigious! I never thought of that. F-o-u-r thousand dollars a\r\nday. Now I do begin to see! But will dead policemen answer?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHaven\xe2\x80\x99t they\xe2\x80\x94up to this time?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, if you put it that way\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPut it any way you want to. Modify it to suit yourself, and my lads\r\nshall still be superior. They won\xe2\x80\x99t eat, they won\xe2\x80\x99t drink\xe2\x80\x94don\xe2\x80\x99t need\r\nthose things; they won\xe2\x80\x99t wink for cash at gambling dens and unlicensed\r\nrum-holes, they won\xe2\x80\x99t spark the scullery maids; and moreover the bands\r\nof toughs that ambuscade them on lonely beats, and cowardly shoot and\r\nknife them will only damage the uniforms and not live long enough to\r\nget more than a momentary satisfaction out of that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, Colonel, if you can furnish policemen, then of course\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly\xe2\x80\x94I can furnish any line of goods that\xe2\x80\x99s wanted. Take the\r\narmy, for instance\xe2\x80\x94now twenty-five thousand men; expense, twenty-two\r\nmillions a year. I will dig up the Romans, I will resurrect the Greeks,\r\nI will furnish the government, for ten millions a year, ten thousand\r\nveterans drawn from the victorious legions of all the ages\xe2\x80\x94soldiers\r\nthat will chase Indians year in and year out on materialized horses,\r\nand cost never a cent for rations or repairs. The armies of Europe cost\r\ntwo billions a year now\xe2\x80\x94I will replace them all for a billion. I will\r\ndig up the trained statesmen of all ages and all climes, and furnish\r\nthis country with a Congress that knows enough to come in out of the\r\nrain\xe2\x80\x94a thing that\xe2\x80\x99s never happened yet, since the Declaration of\r\nIndependence, and never will happen till these practically dead people\r\nare replaced with the genuine article. I will restock the thrones of\r\nEurope with the best brains and the best morals that all the royal\r\nsepulchres of all the centuries can furnish\xe2\x80\x94which isn\xe2\x80\x99t promising very\r\nmuch\xe2\x80\x94and I\xe2\x80\x99ll divide the wages and the civil list, fair and square,\r\nmerely taking my half and\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cColonel, if the half of this is true, there\xe2\x80\x99s millions in\r\nit\xe2\x80\x94millions.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBillions in it\xe2\x80\x94billions; that\xe2\x80\x99s what you mean. Why, look here; the\r\nthing is so close at hand, so imminent, so absolutely immediate, that\r\nif a man were to come to me now and say, Colonel, I am a little short,\r\nand if you could lend me a couple of billion dollars for\xe2\x80\x94come in!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThis in answer to a knock. An energetic looking man bustled in with a\r\nbig pocket-book in his hand, took a paper from it and presented it,\r\nwith the curt remark:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeventeenth and last call\xe2\x80\x94you want to out with that three dollars and\r\nforty cents this time without fail, Colonel Mulberry Sellers.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe Colonel began to slap this pocket and that one, and feel here and\r\nthere and everywhere, muttering:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat _have_ I done with that wallet?\xe2\x80\x94let me see\xe2\x80\x94um\xe2\x80\x94not here, not there\r\n\xe2\x80\x94Oh, I must have left it in the kitchen; I\xe2\x80\x99ll just run and\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo you won\xe2\x80\x99t\xe2\x80\x94you\xe2\x80\x99ll stay right where you are. And you\xe2\x80\x99re going to\r\ndisgorge, too\xe2\x80\x94this time.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington innocently offered to go and look. When he was gone the\r\nColonel said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe fact is, I\xe2\x80\x99ve got to throw myself on your indulgence just this\r\nonce more, Suggs; you see the remittances I was expecting\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHang the remittances\xe2\x80\x94it\xe2\x80\x99s too stale\xe2\x80\x94it won\xe2\x80\x99t answer. Come!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe Colonel glanced about him in despair. Then his face lighted; he ran\r\nto the wall and began to dust off a peculiarly atrocious chromo with\r\nhis handkerchief. Then he brought it reverently, offered it to the\r\ncollector, averted his face and said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTake it, but don\xe2\x80\x99t let me see it go. It\xe2\x80\x99s the sole remaining Rembrandt\r\nthat\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRembrandt be damned, it\xe2\x80\x99s a chromo.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, don\xe2\x80\x99t speak of it so, I beg you. It\xe2\x80\x99s the only really great\r\noriginal, the only supreme example of that mighty school of art which\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cArt! It\xe2\x80\x99s the sickest looking thing I\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe colonel was already bringing another horror and tenderly dusting\r\nit.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTake this one too\xe2\x80\x94the gem of my collection\xe2\x80\x94the only genuine Fra\r\nAngelico that\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIlluminated liver-pad, that\xe2\x80\x99s what it is. Give it here\xe2\x80\x94good day\xe2\x80\x94people\r\nwill think I\xe2\x80\x99ve robbed a\xe2\x80\x99 nigger barber-shop.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAs he slammed the door behind him the Colonel shouted with an anguished\r\naccent\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo please cover them up\xe2\x80\x94don\xe2\x80\x99t let the damp get at them. The delicate\r\ntints in the Angelico\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nBut the man was gone.\r\n\r\nWashington re-appeared and said he had looked everywhere, and so had\r\nMrs. Sellers and the servants, but in vain; and went on to say he\r\nwished he could get his eye on a certain man about this time\xe2\x80\x94no need to\r\nhunt up that pocket-book then. The Colonel\xe2\x80\x99s interest was awake at\r\nonce.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat man?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOne-armed Pete they call him out there\xe2\x80\x94out in the Cherokee country I\r\nmean. Robbed the bank in Tahlequah.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo they have banks in Tahlequah?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes\xe2\x80\x94_a_ bank, anyway. He was suspected of robbing it. Whoever did it\r\ngot away with more than twenty thousand dollars. They offered a reward\r\nof five thousand. I believe I saw that very man, on my way east.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo\xe2\x80\x94is that so?\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI certainly saw a man on the train, the first day I struck the\r\nrailroad, that answered the description pretty exactly\xe2\x80\x94at least as to\r\nclothes and a lacking arm.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy din\xe2\x80\x99t you get him arrested and claim the reward?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI couldn\xe2\x80\x99t. I had to get a requisition, of course. But I meant to stay\r\nby him till I got my chance.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, he left the train during the night some time.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, hang it, that\xe2\x80\x99s too bad.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot so very bad, either.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause he came down to Baltimore in the very train I was in, though I\r\ndidn\xe2\x80\x99t know it in time. As we moved out of the station I saw him going\r\ntoward the iron gate with a satchel in his hand.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood; we\xe2\x80\x99ll catch him. Let\xe2\x80\x99s lay a plan.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSend description to the Baltimore police?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, what are you talking about? No. Do you want them to get the\r\nreward?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat shall we do, then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe Colonel reflected.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll tell you. Put a personal in the Baltimore _Sun_. Word it like\r\nthis:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA. DROP ME A LINE, PETE.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHold on. Which arm has he lost?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe right.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood. Now then\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA. DROP ME A LINE, PETE, EVEN IF YOU HAVE to write with your left\r\nhand. Address X. Y. Z., General Postoffice, Washington. From YOU KNOW\r\nWHO.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x94that\xe2\x80\x99ll fetch him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut he _won\xe2\x80\x99t_ know who\xe2\x80\x94will he?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, but he\xe2\x80\x99ll want to know, won\xe2\x80\x99t he?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, certainly\xe2\x80\x94I didn\xe2\x80\x99t think of that. What made you think of it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cKnowledge of human curiosity. Strong trait, very strong trait.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow I\xe2\x80\x99ll go to my room and write it out and enclose a dollar and tell\r\nthem to print it to the worth of that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER IV.\r\n\r\n\r\np051.jpg (17K)\r\n\r\nThe day wore itself out. After dinner the two friends put in a long and\r\nharassing evening trying to decide what to do with the five thousand\r\ndollars reward which they were going to get when they should find\r\nOne-Armed Pete, and catch him, and prove him to be the right person,\r\nand extradite him, and ship him to Tahlequah in the Indian Territory.\r\nBut there were so many dazzling openings for ready cash that they found\r\nit impossible to make up their minds and keep them made up. Finally,\r\nMrs. Sellers grew very weary of it all, and said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the sense in cooking a rabbit before it\xe2\x80\x99s caught?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThen the matter was dropped, for the time being, and all went to bed.\r\nNext morning, being persuaded by Hawkins, the colonel made drawings and\r\nspecifications and went down and applied for a patent for his toy\r\npuzzle, and Hawkins took the toy itself and started out to see what\r\nchance there might be to do something with it commercially. He did not\r\nhave to go far. In a small old wooden shanty which had once been\r\noccupied as a dwelling by some humble negro family he found a keen-eyed\r\nYankee engaged in repairing cheap chairs and other second-hand\r\nfurniture. This man examined the toy indifferently; attempted to do the\r\npuzzle; found it not so easy as he had expected; grew more interested,\r\nand finally emphatically so; achieved a success at last, and asked:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs it patented?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPatent applied for.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat will answer. What do you want for it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat will it retail for?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, twenty-five cents, I should think.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat will you give for the exclusive right?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI couldn\xe2\x80\x99t give twenty dollars, if I had to pay cash down; but I\xe2\x80\x99ll\r\ntell you what I\xe2\x80\x99ll do. I\xe2\x80\x99ll make it and market it, and pay you five\r\ncents royalty on each one.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWashington sighed. Another dream disappeared; no money in the thing. So\r\nhe said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAll right, take it at that. Draw me a paper.\xe2\x80\x9d He went his way with the\r\npaper, and dropped the matter out of his mind dropped it out to make\r\nroom for further attempts to think out the most promising way to invest\r\nhis half of the reward, in case a partnership investment satisfactory\r\nto both beneficiaries could not be hit upon.\r\n\r\nHe had not been very long at home when Sellers arrived sodden with\r\ngrief and booming with glad excitement\xe2\x80\x94working both these emotions\r\nsuccessfully, sometimes separately, sometimes together. He fell on\r\nHawkins\xe2\x80\x99s neck sobbing, and said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, mourn with me my friend, mourn for my desolate house: death has\r\nsmitten my last kinsman and I am Earl of Rossmore\xe2\x80\x94congratulate me!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe turned to his wife, who had entered while this was going on, put his\r\narms about her and said\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9cYou will bear up, for my sake, my lady\xe2\x80\x94it had\r\nto happen, it was decreed.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe bore up very well, and said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s no great loss. Simon Lathers was a poor well-meaning useless\r\nthing and no account, and his brother never was worth shucks.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe rightful earl continued:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am too much prostrated by these conflicting griefs and joys to be\r\nable to concentrate my mind upon affairs; I will ask our good friend\r\nhere to break the news by wire or post to the Lady Gwendolen and\r\ninstruct her to\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_What_ Lady Gwendolen?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOur poor daughter, who, alas!\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSally Sellers? Mulberry Sellers, are you losing your mind?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x94please do not forget who you are, and who I am; remember your\r\nown dignity, be considerate also of mine. It were best to cease from\r\nusing my family name, now, Lady Rossmore.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGoodness gracious, well, I never! What _am_ I to call you then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn private, the ordinary terms of endearment will still be admissible,\r\nto some degree; but in public it will be more becoming if your ladyship\r\nwill speak _to_ me as my lord, or your lordship, and _of_ me as\r\nRossmore, or the Earl, or his Lordship, and\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, scat! I can\xe2\x80\x99t ever do it, Berry.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut indeed you must, my love\xe2\x80\x94we must live up to our altered position\r\nand submit with what grace we may to its requirements.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, all right, have it your own way; I\xe2\x80\x99ve never set my wishes\r\nagainst your commands yet, Mul\xe2\x80\x94my lord, and it\xe2\x80\x99s late to begin now,\r\nthough to my mind it\xe2\x80\x99s the rottenest foolishness that ever was.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSpoken like my own true wife! There, kiss and be friends again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut\xe2\x80\x94Gwendolen! I don\xe2\x80\x99t know how I am ever going to stand that name.\r\nWhy, a body wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t _know_ Sally Sellers in it. It\xe2\x80\x99s too large for\r\nher; kind of like a cherub in an ulster, and it\xe2\x80\x99s a most outlandish\r\nsort of a name, anyway, to my mind.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99ll not hear her find fault with it, my lady.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s a true word. She takes to any kind of romantic rubbish like she\r\nwas born to it. She never got it from me, that\xe2\x80\x99s sure. And sending her\r\nto that silly college hasn\xe2\x80\x99t helped the matter any\xe2\x80\x94just the other way.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow hear her, Hawkins! Rowena-Ivanhoe College is the selectest and\r\nmost aristocratic seat of learning for young ladies in our country.\r\nUnder no circumstances can a girl get in there unless she is either\r\nvery rich and fashionable or can prove four generations of what may be\r\ncalled American nobility. Castellated college-buildings\xe2\x80\x94towers and\r\nturrets and an imitation moat\xe2\x80\x94and everything about the place named out\r\nof Sir Walter Scott\xe2\x80\x99s books and redolent of royalty and state and\r\nstyle; and all the richest girls keep phaetons, and coachmen in livery,\r\nand riding-horses, with English grooms in plug hats and tight-buttoned\r\ncoats, and top-boots, and a whip-handle without any whip to it, to ride\r\nsixty-three feet behind them\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd they don\xe2\x80\x99t learn a blessed thing, Washington Hawkins, not a single\r\nblessed thing but showy rubbish and un-american pretentiousness. But\r\nsend for the Lady Gwendolen\xe2\x80\x94do; for I reckon the peerage regulations\r\nrequire that she must come home and let on to go into seclusion and\r\nmourn for those Arkansas blatherskites she\xe2\x80\x99s lost.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy darling! Blatherskites? Remember\xe2\x80\x94_noblesse oblige_.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere, there\xe2\x80\x94talk to me in your own tongue, Ross\xe2\x80\x94you don\xe2\x80\x99t know any\r\nother, and you only botch it when you try. Oh, don\xe2\x80\x99t stare\xe2\x80\x94it was a\r\nslip, and no crime; customs of a life-time can\xe2\x80\x99t be dropped in a\r\nsecond. Ross_more_\xe2\x80\x94there, now, be appeased, and go along with you and\r\nattend to Gwendolen. Are you going to write, Washington?\xe2\x80\x94or telegraph?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe will telegraph, dear.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI thought as much,\xe2\x80\x9d my lady muttered, as she left the room. \xe2\x80\x9cWants it\r\nso the address will have to appear on the envelop. It will just make a\r\nfool of that child. She\xe2\x80\x99ll get it, of course, for if there are any\r\nother Sellerses there they\xe2\x80\x99ll not be able to claim it. And just leave\r\nher alone to show it around and make the most of it. Well, maybe she\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nforgivable for that. She\xe2\x80\x99s so poor and they\xe2\x80\x99re so rich, of course she\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nhad her share of snubs from the livery-flunkey sort, and I reckon it\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nonly human to want to get even.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nUncle Dan\xe2\x80\x99l was sent with the telegram; for although a conspicuous\r\nobject in a corner of the drawing-room was a telephone hanging on a\r\ntransmitter, Washington found all attempts to raise the central office\r\nvain. The Colonel grumbled something about its being \xe2\x80\x9c_always_ out of\r\norder when you\xe2\x80\x99ve got particular and especial use for it,\xe2\x80\x9d but he\r\ndidn\xe2\x80\x99t explain that one of the reasons for this was that the thing was\r\nonly a dummy and hadn\xe2\x80\x99t any wire attached to it. And yet the Colonel\r\noften used it\xe2\x80\x94when visitors were present\xe2\x80\x94and seemed to get messages\r\nthrough it. Mourning paper and a seal were ordered, then the friends\r\ntook a rest.\r\n\r\nNext afternoon, while Hawkins, by request, draped Andrew Jackson\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nportrait with crape, the rightful earl, wrote off the family\r\nbereavement to the usurper in England\xe2\x80\x94a letter which we have already\r\nread. He also, by letter to the village authorities at Duffy\xe2\x80\x99s Corners,\r\nArkansas, gave order that the remains of the late twins be embalmed by\r\nsome St. Louis expert and shipped at once to the usurper\xe2\x80\x94with bill.\r\nThen he drafted out the Rossmore arms and motto on a great sheet of\r\nbrown paper, and he and Hawkins took it to Hawkins\xe2\x80\x99s Yankee\r\nfurniture-mender and at the end of an hour came back with a couple of\r\nstunning hatchments, which they nailed up on the front of the\r\nhouse\xe2\x80\x94attractions calculated to draw, and they did; for it was mainly\r\nan idle and shiftless negro neighborhood, with plenty of ragged\r\nchildren and indolent dogs to spare for a point of interest like that,\r\nand keep on sparing them for it, days and days together.\r\n\r\nThe new earl found\xe2\x80\x94without surprise\xe2\x80\x94this society item in the evening\r\npaper, and cut it out and scrapbooked it:\r\n\r\nBy a recent bereavement our esteemed fellow citizen, Colonel Mulberry\r\nSellers, Perpetual Member-at-large of the Diplomatic Body, succeeds, as\r\nrightful lord, to the great earldom of Rossmore, third by order of\r\nprecedence in the earldoms of Great Britain, and will take early\r\nmeasures, by suit in the House of Lords, to wrest the title and estates\r\nfrom the present usurping holder of them. Until the season of mourning\r\nis past, the usual Thursday evening receptions at Rossmore Towers will\r\nbe discontinued.\r\n\r\n\r\nLady Rossmore\xe2\x80\x99s comment\xe2\x80\x94to herself:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReceptions! People who don\xe2\x80\x99t rightly know him may think he is\r\ncommonplace, but to my mind he is one of the most unusual men I ever\r\nsaw. As for suddenness and capacity in imagining things, his beat don\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nexist, I reckon. As like as not it wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have occurred to anybody\r\nelse to name this poor old rat-trap Rossmore Towers, but it just comes\r\nnatural to him. Well, no doubt it\xe2\x80\x99s a blessed thing to have an\r\nimagination that can always make you satisfied, no matter how you are\r\nfixed. Uncle Dave Hopkins used to always say, \xe2\x80\x98Turn me into John\r\nCalvin, and I want to know which place I\xe2\x80\x99m going to; turn me into\r\nMulberry Sellers and I don\xe2\x80\x99t care.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe rightful earl\xe2\x80\x99s comment\xe2\x80\x94to himself:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a beautiful name, beautiful. Pity I didn\xe2\x80\x99t think of it before I\r\nwrote the usurper. But I\xe2\x80\x99ll be ready for him when he answers.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER V.\r\n\r\n\r\nNo answer to that telegram; no arriving daughter. Yet nobody showed any\r\nuneasiness or seemed surprised; that is, nobody but Washington. After\r\nthree days of waiting, he asked Lady Rossmore what she supposed the\r\ntrouble was. She answered, tranquilly:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, it\xe2\x80\x99s some notion of hers, you never can tell. She\xe2\x80\x99s a Sellers, all\r\nthrough\xe2\x80\x94at least in some of her ways; and a Sellers can\xe2\x80\x99t tell you\r\nbeforehand what he\xe2\x80\x99s going to do, because he don\xe2\x80\x99t know himself till\r\nhe\xe2\x80\x99s done it. _She\xe2\x80\x99s_ all right; no occasion to worry about _her_. When\r\nshe\xe2\x80\x99s ready she\xe2\x80\x99ll come or she\xe2\x80\x99ll write, and you can\xe2\x80\x99t tell which, till\r\nit\xe2\x80\x99s happened.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIt turned out to be a letter. It was handed in at that moment, and was\r\nreceived by the mother without trembling hands or feverish eagerness,\r\nor any other of the manifestations common in the case of long delayed\r\nanswers to imperative telegrams. She polished her glasses with\r\ntranquility and thoroughness, pleasantly gossiping along, the while,\r\nthen opened the letter and began to read aloud:\r\n\r\nKENILWORTH KEEP, REDGAUNTLET HALL,\r\nROWENA-IVANHOE COLLEGE, THURSDAY.\r\n\r\n\r\nDEAR PRECIOUS MAMMA ROSSMORE:\r\n\r\nOh, the joy of it!\xe2\x80\x94you can\xe2\x80\x99t think. They had always turned up their\r\nnoses at our pretentions, you know; and I had fought back as well as I\r\ncould by turning up mine at theirs. They always said it might be\r\nsomething great and fine to be the rightful Shadow of an earldom, but\r\nto merely be shadow _of_ a shadow, and two or three times removed at\r\nthat\xe2\x80\x94pooh-pooh! And I always retorted that not to be able to show four\r\ngenerations of American-Colonial-Dutch\r\nPeddler-and-Salt-Cod-McAllister-Nobility might be endurable, but to\r\n_have_ to confess such an origin\xe2\x80\x94pfew-few! Well, the telegram, it was\r\njust a cyclone! The messenger came right into the great Rob Roy Hall of\r\nAudience, as excited as he could be, singing out, \xe2\x80\x9cDispatch for Lady\r\nGwendolen Sellers!\xe2\x80\x9d and you ought to have seen that simpering\r\nchattering assemblage of pinchbeck aristocrats, turn to stone! I was\r\noff in the corner, of course, by myself\xe2\x80\x94it\xe2\x80\x99s where Cinderella belongs.\r\nI took the telegram and read it, and tried to faint\xe2\x80\x94and I could have\r\ndone it if I had had any preparation, but it was all so sudden, you\r\nknow\xe2\x80\x94but no matter, I did the next best thing: I put my handkerchief to\r\nmy eyes and fled sobbing to my room, dropping the telegram as I\r\nstarted. I released one corner of my eye a moment\xe2\x80\x94just enough to see\r\nthe herd swarm for the telegram\xe2\x80\x94and then continued my broken-hearted\r\nflight just as happy as a bird.\r\n\r\nThen the visits of condolence began, and I had to accept the loan of\r\nMiss Augusta-Templeton-Ashmore Hamilton\xe2\x80\x99s quarters because the press\r\nwas so great and there isn\xe2\x80\x99t room for three and a cat in mine. And I\xe2\x80\x99ve\r\nbeen holding a Lodge of Sorrow ever since and defending myself against\r\npeople\xe2\x80\x99s attempts to claim kin. And do you know, the very first girl to\r\nfetch her tears and sympathy to my market was that foolish Skimperton\r\ngirl who has always snubbed me so shamefully and claimed lordship and\r\nprecedence of the whole college because some ancestor of hers, some\r\ntime or other, was a McAllister. Why it was like the bottom bird in the\r\nmenagerie putting on airs because its head ancestor was a pterodactyl.\r\n\r\nBut the ger-reatest triumph of all was\xe2\x80\x94guess. But you\xe2\x80\x99ll never. This is\r\nit. That little fool and two others have always been fussing and\r\nfretting over which was entitled to precedence\xe2\x80\x94by rank, you know.\r\nThey\xe2\x80\x99ve nearly starved themselves at it; for each claimed the right to\r\ntake precedence of all the college in leaving the table, and so neither\r\nof them ever finished her dinner, but broke off in the middle and tried\r\nto get out ahead of the others. Well, after my first day\xe2\x80\x99s grief and\r\nseclusion\xe2\x80\x94I was fixing up a mourning dress you see\xe2\x80\x94I appeared at the\r\npublic table again, and then\xe2\x80\x94what do you think? Those three fluffy\r\ngoslings sat there contentedly, and squared up the long famine\xe2\x80\x94lapped\r\nand lapped, munched and munched, ate and ate, till the gravy appeared\r\nin their eyes\xe2\x80\x94humbly waiting for the Lady Gwendolen to take precedence\r\nand move out first, you see!\r\n\r\nOh, yes, I\xe2\x80\x99ve been having a darling good time. And do you know, not one\r\nof these collegians has had the cruelty to ask me how I came by my new\r\nname. With some, this is due to charity, but with the others it isn\xe2\x80\x99t.\r\nThey refrain, not from native kindness but from educated discretion. I\r\neducated them.\r\n\r\nWell, as soon as I shall have settled up what\xe2\x80\x99s left of the old scores\r\nand snuffed up a few more of those pleasantly intoxicating clouds of\r\nincense, I shall pack and depart homeward. Tell papa I am as fond of\r\nhim as I am of my new name. I couldn\xe2\x80\x99t put it stronger than that. What\r\nan inspiration it was! But inspirations come easy to him.\r\n\r\n\r\nThese, from your loving daughter,\r\nGWENDOLEN.\r\n\r\n\r\nHawkins reached for the letter and glanced over it.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood hand,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cand full of confidence and animation, and goes\r\nracing right along. She\xe2\x80\x99s bright\xe2\x80\x94that\xe2\x80\x99s plain.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, they\xe2\x80\x99re all bright\xe2\x80\x94the Sellerses. Anyway, they would be, if there\r\nwere any. Even those poor Latherses would have been bright if they had\r\nbeen Sellerses; I mean full blood. Of course they had a Sellers strain\r\nin them\xe2\x80\x94a big strain of it, too\xe2\x80\x94but being a Bland dollar don\xe2\x80\x99t make it\r\na _dollar_ just the same.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe seventh day after the date of the telegram Washington came dreaming\r\ndown to breakfast and was set wide awake by an electrical spasm of\r\npleasure.\r\n\r\nHere was the most beautiful young creature he had ever seen in his\r\nlife. It was Sally Sellers Lady Gwendolen; she had come in the night.\r\nAnd it seemed to him that her clothes were the prettiest and the\r\ndaintiest he had ever looked upon, and the most exquisitely contrived\r\nand fashioned and combined, as to decorative trimmings, and fixings,\r\nand melting harmonies of color. It was only a morning dress, and\r\ninexpensive, but he confessed to himself, in the English common to\r\nCherokee Strip, that it was a \xe2\x80\x9ccorker.\xe2\x80\x9d And now, as he perceived, the\r\nreason why the Sellers household poverties and sterilities had been\r\nmade to blossom like the rose, and charm the eye and satisfy the\r\nspirit, stood explained; here was the magician; here in the midst of\r\nher works, and furnishing in her own person the proper accent and\r\nclimaxing finish of the whole.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy daughter, Major Hawkins\xe2\x80\x94come home to mourn; flown home at the call\r\nof affliction to help the authors of her being bear the burden of\r\nbereavement. She was very fond of the late earl\xe2\x80\x94idolized him, sir,\r\nidolized him\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, father, I\xe2\x80\x99ve never seen him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTrue\xe2\x80\x94she\xe2\x80\x99s right, I was thinking of another\xe2\x80\x94er\xe2\x80\x94of her mother\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_I_ idolized that smoked haddock?\xe2\x80\x94that sentimental, spiritless\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI was thinking of myself! Poor noble fellow, we were inseparable com\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHear the man! Mulberry Sel\xe2\x80\x94Mul\xe2\x80\x94Rossmore\xe2\x80\x94hang the troublesome name I\r\ncan never\xe2\x80\x94if I\xe2\x80\x99ve heard you say once, I\xe2\x80\x99ve heard you say a thousand\r\ntimes that if that poor sheep\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI was thinking of\xe2\x80\x94of\xe2\x80\x94I don\xe2\x80\x99t know who I was thinking of, and it\r\ndoesn\xe2\x80\x99t make any difference anyway; _some_body idolized him, I\r\nrecollect it as if it were yesterday; and\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFather, I am going to shake hands with Major Hawkins, and let the\r\nintroduction work along and catch up at its leisure. I remember you\r\nvery well in deed, Major Hawkins, although I was a little child when I\r\nsaw you last; and I am very, very glad indeed to see you again and have\r\nyou in our house as one of us;\xe2\x80\x9d and beaming in his face she finished\r\nher cordial shake with the hope that he had not forgotten her.\r\n\r\n\r\np061.jpg (29K)\r\n\r\nHe was prodigiously pleased by her outspoken heartiness, and wanted to\r\nrepay her by assuring her that he remembered her, and not only that but\r\nbetter even than he remembered his own children, but the facts would\r\nnot quite warrant this; still, he stumbled through a tangled sentence\r\nwhich answered just as well, since the purport of it was an awkward and\r\nunintentional confession that her extraordinary beauty had so stupefied\r\nhim that he hadn\xe2\x80\x99t got back to his bearings, yet, and therefore\r\ncouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be certain as to whether he remembered her at all or not. The\r\nspeech made him her friend; it couldn\xe2\x80\x99t well help it.\r\n\r\nIn truth the beauty of this fair creature was of a rare type, and may\r\nwell excuse a moment of our time spent in its consideration. It did not\r\nconsist in the _fact_ that she had eyes, nose, mouth, chin, hair, ears,\r\nit consisted in their arrangement. In true beauty, more depends upon\r\nright location and judicious distribution of feature than upon\r\nmultiplicity of them. So also as regards color. The very combination of\r\ncolors which in a volcanic irruption would add beauty to a landscape\r\nmight detach it from a girl. Such was Gwendolen Sellers.\r\n\r\nThe family circle being completed by Gwendolen\xe2\x80\x99s arrival, it was\r\ndecreed that the official mourning should now begin; that it should\r\nbegin at six o\xe2\x80\x99clock every evening, (the dinner hour,) and end with the\r\ndinner.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a grand old line, major, a sublime old line, and deserves to be\r\nmourned for, almost royally; almost imperially, I may say. Er\xe2\x80\x94Lady\r\nGwendolen\xe2\x80\x94but she\xe2\x80\x99s gone; never mind; I wanted my Peerage; I\xe2\x80\x99ll fetch\r\nit myself, presently, and show you a thing or two that will give you a\r\nrealizing idea of what our house is. I\xe2\x80\x99ve been glancing through Burke,\r\nand I find that of William the Conqueror\xe2\x80\x99s sixty-four natural ch\xe2\x80\x94my\r\ndear, would you mind getting me that book? It\xe2\x80\x99s on the escritoire in\r\nour boudoir. Yes, as I was saying, there\xe2\x80\x99s only St. Albans, Buccleugh\r\nand Grafton ahead of us on the list\xe2\x80\x94all the rest of the British\r\nnobility are in procession behind us. Ah, thanks, my lady. Now then, we\r\nturn to William, and we find\xe2\x80\x94letter for XYZ? Oh, splendid\xe2\x80\x94when\xe2\x80\x99d you\r\nget it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLast night; but I was asleep before you came, you were out so late;\r\nand when I came to breakfast Miss Gwendolen\xe2\x80\x94well, she knocked\r\neverything out of me, you know\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWonderful girl, wonderful; her great origin is detectable in her step,\r\nher carriage, her features\xe2\x80\x94but what does he _say?_ Come, this is\r\nexciting.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI haven\xe2\x80\x99t read it\xe2\x80\x94er\xe2\x80\x94Rossm\xe2\x80\x94Mr. Rossm\xe2\x80\x94er\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cM\xe2\x80\x99lord! Just cut it short like that. It\xe2\x80\x99s the English way. I\xe2\x80\x99ll open\r\nit. Ah, now let\xe2\x80\x99s see.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nA. TO YOU KNOW WHO. Think I know you. Wait ten days. Coming to\r\nWashington.\r\n\r\n\r\nThe excitement died out of both men\xe2\x80\x99s faces. There was a brooding\r\nsilence for a while, then the younger one said with a sigh:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, _we_ can\xe2\x80\x99t wait ten days for the money.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo\xe2\x80\x94the man\xe2\x80\x99s unreasonable; we are down to the bed rock, financially\r\nspeaking.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf we could explain to him in some way, that we are so situated that\r\ntime is of the utmost importance to us\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes\xe2\x80\x94yes, that\xe2\x80\x99s it\xe2\x80\x94and so if it would be as convenient for him to come\r\nat once it would be a great accommodation to us, and one which we\xe2\x80\x94which\r\nwe\xe2\x80\x94which we\xe2\x80\x94wh\xe2\x80\x94well, which we should sincerely appreciate\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s it\xe2\x80\x94and most gladly reciprocate\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly\xe2\x80\x94that\xe2\x80\x99ll fetch him. Worded right, if he\xe2\x80\x99s a _man_\xe2\x80\x94got any of\r\nthe _feelings_ of a man, _sympathies_ and all that, he\xe2\x80\x99ll be here\r\ninside of twenty-four hours. Pen and paper\xe2\x80\x94come, we\xe2\x80\x99ll get right at\r\nit.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nBetween them they framed twenty-two different advertisements, but none\r\nwas satisfactory. A main fault in all of them was urgency. That feature\r\nwas very troublesome: if made prominent, it was calculated to excite\r\nPete\xe2\x80\x99s suspicion; if modified below the suspicion-point it was flat and\r\nmeaningless. Finally the Colonel resigned, and said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have noticed, in such literary experiences as I have had, that one\r\nof the most taking things to do is to conceal your meaning when you are\r\n_trying_ to conceal it. Whereas, if you go at literature with a free\r\nconscience and nothing to conceal, you can turn out a book, every time,\r\nthat the very elect can\xe2\x80\x99t understand. They all do.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThen Hawkins resigned also, and the two agreed that they must manage to\r\nwait the ten days some how or other. Next, they caught a ray of cheer:\r\nsince they had something definite to go upon, now, they could probably\r\nborrow money on the reward\xe2\x80\x94enough, at any rate, to tide them over till\r\nthey got it; and meantime the materializing recipe would be perfected,\r\nand then good bye to trouble for good and all.\r\n\r\nThe next day, May the tenth, a couple of things happened\xe2\x80\x94among others.\r\nThe remains of the noble Arkansas twins left our shores for England,\r\nconsigned to Lord Rossmore, and Lord Rossmore\xe2\x80\x99s son, Kirkcudbright\r\nLlanover Marjoribanks Sellers Viscount Berkeley, sailed from Liverpool\r\nfor America to place the reversion of the earldom in the hands of the\r\nrightful peer, Mulberry Sellers, of Rossmore Towers in the District of\r\nColumbia, U. S. A.\r\n\r\nThese two impressive shipments would meet and part in mid-Atlantic,\r\nfive days later, and give no sign.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER VI.\r\n\r\n\r\nIn the course of time the twins arrived and were delivered to their\r\ngreat kinsman.
